<P STYLE="margin: 0; text-align: right"><FONT STYLE="font-family: Arial, 
Helvetica, Sans-Serif; font-size: 8pt"><B>Exhibit 99.1</B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin: 0; text-align: right">&nbsp;</P>
<P STYLE="margin: 0; text-align: right"></P>
<P STYLE="font: 12pt Arial, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0">&nbsp;</P>
<P STYLE="font: 12pt Arial, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0"></P>
<P STYLE="font: 12pt Arial, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0"></P>
<P STYLE="font: 12pt Arial, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0"></P>
<P STYLE="font: 12pt Arial, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0"></P>
<P STYLE="font: 12pt Arial, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0"><B>Energy Fuels 
Announces High-Grade Uranium Intercepts at the Canyon
Mine</B></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Arial, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 9.75pt 0">LAKEWOOD, 
CO, Aug. 18, 2016 /CNW/ -&nbsp;<B>Energy Fuels Inc.
(NYSE MKT: UUUU; TSX: EFR) (&quot;Energy Fuels&quot; or the 
&quot;Company&quot;)</B>, a leading producer of uranium in the United
States, is pleased to announce that it has intercepted several large and high-
grade areas of mineralization at its Canyon Mine,
a conventional uranium mine located in northern Arizona, USA.&nbsp;</P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Arial, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 9.75pt 0">The Company
is currently pursuing an underground delineation
core drilling program from a station located at a depth of approximately 1,000 
feet below the surface.&nbsp; To date, thirteen
(13) core holes have been drilled, and most have encountered uranium 
mineralization in multiple levels throughout the deposit,
including 8.5-feet of mineralization with an average grade of 6.88% 
eU<SUB>3</SUB>O<SUB>8</SUB>, 48.0-feet of mineralization with
an average grade of 1.02% eU<SUB>3</SUB>O<SUB>8</SUB>, and 35-feet of 
mineralization with an average grade of 1.39% eU<SUB>3</SUB>O<SUB>8</SUB>.
&nbsp;The Company expects to drill a total of fifteen (15) core holes from the 
first station during the current drilling program,
which is expected to be followed up by additional delineation drilling from a 
second station later this year.</P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Arial, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 9.75pt 0">The table 
below summarizes the data for the ten (10) best
individual intercepts that the Company has encountered to date:</P>
<TABLE CELLSPACING="0" CELLPADDING="0" STYLE="width: 100%; font: 10pt Arial, 
Helvetica, Sans-Serif">
<TR>
    <TD STYLE="border-bottom: black 1pt solid; padding: 1.5pt"><FONT

<P STYLE="font: 10pt Arial, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 9.75pt 0; text-
indent: 0.5in">&nbsp;</P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Arial, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 9.75pt 0">All holes 
were logged for gamma by trained Company personnel
to calculate eU<SUB>3</SUB>O<SUB>8</SUB>%.&nbsp; Gamma logging tools were 
calibrated prior to the drilling program and verified
by an independent 3<SUP>rd</SUP> party geophysicist.&nbsp; Samples from the 
zones showing high eU<SUB>3</SUB>O<SUB>8</SUB>% assay
values are currently being sampled and sent to the Company's White Mesa Mill for
further verification.</P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Arial, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 9.75pt 0">According 
to a June 27, 2012 technical report (&quot;Technical
Report&quot;) prepared in accordance with National Instrument 43-101 &ndash; 
<I>Standards of Disclosure for Mineral Projects</I>
(&quot;NI 43-101&quot;), the Canyon deposit contains 83,000 tons of Inferred 
Mineral Resources with an average grade of 0.98% eU<SUB>3</SUB>O<SUB>8</SUB>,
containing 1.63 million pounds of uranium.&nbsp; The existing Technical Report 
was based on the results of surface drilling.&nbsp;
The current underground drilling program is intended to further define and 
delineate the uranium resources in the Canyon deposit
&ndash; and to potentially expand and upgrade the resources &ndash; above what 
are described in the Technical Report.&nbsp; If
required, the Company expects to have an updated Technical Report prepared for 
the Canyon deposit, in accordance with NI 43-101.</P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Arial, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 9.75pt 0">In addition
to the delineation drilling, the Company is also
continuing to sink an 8-foot by 20-foot mine shaft, which will be used to access
the deposit.&nbsp; The shaft is currently at a
depth of approximately 1,100 feet.</P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Arial, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 9.75pt 0">Stephen P. 
Antony, President and CEO of Energy Fuels stated:&nbsp;
&quot;So far, the results of the underground drill program at the Canyon deposit
are very positive.&nbsp; The uranium grades, thicknesses,
and continuities we have encountered at this stage of our delineation drilling 
program are confirming our high expectations for
the deposit.&nbsp; Furthermore, as we extend core holes beyond the known zones 
of mineralization, additional high-grade uranium
resources are being identified that are expanding the size of the deposit beyond
what was described in the Technical Report.&nbsp;</P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Arial, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 9.75pt 0">&quot;We 
have long known that the Canyon deposit boasts world-class
uranium grades, and we have the potential to increase the tonnage to be mined 
through underground delineation drilling.&nbsp; Historically,
uranium produced from other similar deposits in northern Arizona was low-cost 
and competitive globally with other low-cost underground
uranium mines, including mines in Canada.&nbsp; In addition, the Canyon Mine 
enjoys other important advantages.&nbsp; It is fully
licensed and permitted.&nbsp; It is at a very advanced stage of construction, 
with all surface development completed and the shaft
is close to being complete.&nbsp; And, the mine is located within economic 
trucking distance of Energy Fuels' White Mesa Mill,
which is licensed, operating, and has the capacity to process the Canyon 
material into finished yellowcake that can be sold to
global nuclear utilities.&nbsp; We look forward to completing our current drill 
program, potentially performing future delineation
drill programs, and continuing to confirm the size and quality of the 
resources.&quot;</P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Arial, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 9.75pt 0"><B><I>About
Energy Fuels:&nbsp; </I></B><I>Energy Fuels is
a leading integrated US-based uranium mining company, supplying 
U<SUB>3</SUB>O<SUB>8</SUB> to major nuclear utilities.&nbsp; Energy
Fuels holds three of America's key uranium production centers, the White Mesa 
Mill in Utah, the Nichols Ranch Processing Facility
in Wyoming, and the Alta Mesa Project in Texas.&nbsp; The White Mesa Mill is the
only conventional uranium mill operating in the
U.S. today and has a licensed capacity of over 8 million pounds of 
U<SUB>3</SUB>O<SUB>8</SUB> per year.&nbsp; The Nichols Ranch
Processing Facility is an ISR production center with a licensed capacity of 2 
million pounds of U<SUB>3</SUB>O<SUB>8</SUB> per
year.&nbsp; Alta Mesa is an ISR production center currently on care and 
maintenance.&nbsp; Energy Fuels also has the largest NI
43-101 compliant uranium resource portfolio in the U.S. among producers, and 
uranium mining projects located in a number of Western
U.S. states, including one producing ISR project, mines on standby, and mineral 
properties in various stages of permitting and
development.&nbsp; The Company's common shares are listed on the NYSE MKT under 
the trading symbol &quot;UUUU&quot;, and on the
Toronto Stock Exchange under the trading symbol &quot;EFR&quot;.</I></P>
<P STYLE="font: 10pt Arial, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 9.75pt 
0"><B><I>Stephen P. Antony, P.E., President &amp; CEO of Energy
Fuels</I></B><I>, is a Qualified Person as defined by Canadian National 
Instrument 43-101 and has reviewed and approved the technical
disclosure contained in this news release, including sampling, analytical, and 
test data underlying such disclosure.&nbsp; </I></P>
